From Giacomo.Cau at GeneraliGroup.com  Sun Feb  1 18:16:06 2009
From: Giacomo.Cau at GeneraliGroup.com (Cau Giacomo)
Date: Sun, 1 Feb 2009 18:16:06 +0100
Subject: [Stratego Users] Multiline java comments
Message-ID: <CD2A92F857252C46993EE29535FB8B5203655C2F@BEMAILEXTV01.corp.generali.net>

multiline java comments aren't dealed at the best
 
# cat > p.java
class p {
     /* first line
      * second line
      */
     int a = 1;
     // one line
     int b /* inline */ = 2;
 }
# parse-java --preserve-comments -i p.java | pp-java
class p
{
  /* first line
      * second line
      */ int a = 1;
  // one line
  int b = 2;
}

 
the first comment loses the \n
the second is ok
the third dissapears :-)
 
i think the first case is due to the definition given (java-front-0.9pre18236) in the module
 
   syntax/src/languages/java-15/lexical/Comments.sdf

 
maybe it could be easily adapted as
 
   "/*" CommentPart* "*/" [\ \t]* LineTerminator? -> Comment
 
for what regards the third case I don't know if something could be done easily.
 
bye

		Giacomo

 
ps: the hack for io-java2java-wrap with preserve-comments now is tested 
 
imports
    libstratego-lib
    libjava-front
    libstratego-sglr
strategies
   main = io-java2java-wrap-pc(id)
   io-java2java-wrap-pc(s) =
      io-stream-wrap(io-java2java-pc(s))
   io-java2java-pc(s) =
      io-java2java-pc(s | "CompilationUnit")
   io-java2java-pc(s | sort) =
      ?(<id>, fout)
      ; parse-java-stream-pt(|sort, <get-config <+ !stdin()> "-i")
      ; asfix-anno-comments
      ; implode-asfix
      ; s
      ; pp-java-stream(|fout)
      ; <fputs> ("\n", fout)

Hi, folks.

I've been trying to install Stratego/XT for a while (AspectJ-front should be
further installed). However, I always get stuck at the same point. I have
tried it in different machines, all running Ubuntu 8.10 Linux.

According to the installation directions, I should run the sequence "aterm
-> sdf-bundle -> strategoxt -> java-front -> aspectj-front". The first two
steps succeed (i.e. aterm and sdf-bundle packages). For strategoxt, I'm able
to run the "configure" successfully. However, when I run the "make", the
installation freezes at the point shown below.

gcc -Wall -Wno-unused-label -Wno-unused-variable -Wno-unused-function

From a.serebrenik at tue.nl  Wed Feb  4 23:34:23 2009
From: a.serebrenik at tue.nl (Serebrenik, A.)
Date: Wed, 4 Feb 2009 23:34:23 +0100
Subject: [Stratego Users] Call for Papers: 2nd International Conference on
 Software Language Engineering
Message-ID: <7DF2365FF07C0E4E89419D65CCC93C9E015BEB8353CA@EXCHANGE11.campus.tue.nl>


__________________________________________________________________
                       Call for Papers - SLE 2009

    2nd International Conference on Software Language Engineering

                     http://planet-sl.org/sle2009

                 Denver, Colorado, October 5-6, 2009

___________________________________________________________________

           Co-located with 12th International Conference on
    Model-Driven Engineering Languages and Systems (MODELS 2009)
                and 8th International Conference on
     Generative Programming and Component Engineering (GPCE 2009)

Proceedings will be published in the LNCS series (subject to
Springer's approval).

The 2nd International Conference on Software Language Engineering (SLE)
is devoted to topics related to artificial languages in software
engineering. SLE's foremost mission is to encourage and organize
communication between communities that have traditionally looked
at software languages from different, more specialized, and yet
complementary perspectives. SLE emphasizes the fundamental notion
of languages as opposed to any realization in specific "technical
spaces". SLE 2009 will be co-located with the 12th IEEE/ACM
International Conference on Model-Driven Engineering Languages and
Systems (MODELS 2009).


Scope
-----

The term 'software language' comprises all sorts of artificial
languages used in software development including general-purpose
programming languages, domain-specific languages, modeling and
meta-modeling languages, data models, and ontologies. Used in its
broadest sense, examples include modeling languages such as
UML-based and domain-specific modeling languages, business process
modeling languages, and web application modeling languages.  The
term 'software language' also comprises APIs and collections of
design patterns that are implicitly defined languages.

Software language engineering is the application of a systematic,
disciplined, quantifiable approach to the development, use, and
maintenance of these languages. Thus, the SLE conference is
concerned with all phases of the life cycle of software languages;
these include the design, implementation, documentation, testing,
deployment, evolution, recovery, and retirement of languages. Of
special interest are tools, techniques, methods and formalisms that
support these activities. In particular, tools are often based on
or even automatically generated from a formal description of the
language. Hence, of special interest is the treatment of language
descriptions as software artifacts, akin to programs - while paying
attention to the special status of language descriptions, subject
to tailored engineering principles and methods for modularization,
refactoring, refinement, composition, versioning, co-evolution,
and analysis.


Topics of interest
------------------

We solicit high-quality contributions in the area of SLE ranging
from theoretical and conceptual contributions to tools, techniques
and frameworks that support the aforementioned life cycle activities.
Some examples of tools, techniques, applications, and problems are
listed below in order to clarify the types of contributions sought
by SLE.

* Formalisms used in designing and specifying languages and tools
  that analyze such language descriptions.

* Language implementation techniques, grammar-based and
  metamodel-based.


* Program and model transformation tools.

* Composition, integration, and mapping tools for managing different
  aspects of software languages or different manifestations of a
  given language.

* Language evolution.

* Approaches to the elicitation, specification, and verification of
  requirements for software languages.

* Language development frameworks, methodologies, techniques, best
  practices, and tools for the broader language life cycle covering
  phases such as analysis, testing, and documentation.

* Design challenges in SLE.

* Applications of languages including innovative domain-specific
  languages or "little" languages

Do note that this list is not exclusive and many examples of tools,
techniques, approaches have not been listed. Please visit the
conference web site to see a more elaborate description of the
topics of interests. The program committee chairs encourage potential
contributors to contact them with questions about the scope and
topics of interest of SLE.


Paper Submission
----------------

We solicit the following types of papers:

 * Research papers. These should report a substantial research
   contribution to SLE and/or successful application of SLE
   techniques. Full paper submissions must not exceed 20 pages.

 * Short papers. These may describe interesting or thought-provoking
   concepts that are not yet fully developed or evaluated, make an
   initial contribution to challenging research issues in SLE, or
   discuss and analyze controversial issues in the field. These papers
   must not exceed 10 pages.

 * Tool demonstration papers. Because of SLE's ample interest in
   tools, we seek papers that present software tools related to the
   field of SLE. These papers will accompany a tool demonstration to
   be given at the conference. These papers must not exceed 10
   pages. The selection criteria include the originality of the tool,
   its innovative aspects, the relevance of the tool to SLE, and the
   maturity of the tool. Submissions may also include an appendix
   (that will not be published) containing additional screen-shots and
   discussion of the proposed demonstration.

 * Mini-tutorial papers. SLE is composed of various research areas,
   such as grammarware, modelware, language schemas, and semantic
   technologies. The cross product of attendees at SLE creates a
   situation where the contribution from one session may be difficult
   to understand by those not initiated to the area. To help unite the
   various communitues of SLE 2009, mini-tutorials are solicited
   that provide discussion points for mapping common ideas between the
   area and differentiating among variations. A mini-tutorial submisson
   should be between 15 and 20 pages.

Submitted articles must not have been previously published or currently
be submitted for publication elsewhere. All submitted papers will be
closely reviewed by at least three members of the program committee. All
accepted papers will be made available at the conference in the
pre-proceedings and published in the post-proceedings of the conference,
which will appear in Springer's Lecture Notes in Computer Science series.
Authors will have the opportunity to revise their accepted paper for the
pre- and post-proceedings.

All papers must be formatted by following Springer's LNCS style and
must be submitted using EasyChair (open early June):

     http://www.easychair.org/conferences/?conf=sle09

Further details regarding submission can be found on the SLE web page:

     http://planet-sl.org/sle2009

From sandervermolen at gmail.com  Thu Feb 12 17:56:03 2009
From: sandervermolen at gmail.com (Sander Vermolen)
Date: Thu, 12 Feb 2009 17:56:03 +0100
Subject: [Stratego Users] List primitives
Message-ID: <721433520902120856v633c1b48x178f252c70259773@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

I am using stratego for processing rather large amounts of data
(databases). Doing this, I am currently stuck with a list problem:
I am trying to decompose a list into chunks of fixed size. So for
example, if the chunk size is 2, I would like to transform

[1,2,3,4,5]
into
[[1,2],[3,4],[5]]

In practice, the chunk size is about a thousand elements and the
list's length about one million.

A first, naive implementation using split-at and recursion uses
ridiculous amounts of memory space (even after completion) and a lot
of time. I am now trying to implement the strategy using list
primitives only. list-fold appeared to be the most suitable option,
considering the other two are length and list-loop. Unfortunately I do
not understand list-fold's behavior. I get this from the stratego
shell:

<list-fold(debug | 4)> [5,6,7]
4
4
4
And as result (surprise, surprise): 4

Apparently it is the start element 4, which is used over and over
again. However, I would at least expect to be able to use the list
elements in the given strategy. Preferably a tuple like foldl and
foldr do.
Did I miss something here? Or does anyone know a better way of dealing
with large lists?

Thanks in advance,
Sander

From martin.bravenboer at gmail.com  Thu Feb 12 18:06:20 2009
From: martin.bravenboer at gmail.com (Martin Bravenboer)
Date: Thu, 12 Feb 2009 09:06:20 -0800
Subject: [Stratego Users] List primitives
In-Reply-To: <721433520902120856v633c1b48x178f252c70259773@mail.gmail.com>
References: <721433520902120856v633c1b48x178f252c70259773@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <2074242c0902120906m2e691e71ja2924e1f6311c253@mail.gmail.com>

Hi Sander,

> Did I miss something here? Or does anyone know a better way of dealing
> with large lists?

I'm not sure it's a wise idea to use ATerm lists for this, but
list-fold should at least be fairly efficient in terms of memory.
List-fold was introduced to avoid the creation of intermediate tuples,
as the other fold strategies do. List-fold a normal fold, where the
strategy parameter is a strategy taking a term argument. The example
from the testsuite will probably clarify this:

-----------------------------------------------------------
  list-fold-tests =
    let add-helper(|x) = <add> (x, <id>)
        mul-helper(|x) = <mul> (x, <id>)
     in id

    ; apply-test(!"list-fold 1", list-fold(add-helper | 0), ![], !0)
    ; apply-test(!"list-fold 2", list-fold(add-helper | 0), ![1], !1)
    ; apply-test(!"list-fold 3", list-fold(add-helper | 0), ![1, 2, 3, 4], !10)
    ; apply-test(!"list-fold 4", list-fold(mul-helper | 1), ![1, 2, 3, 4], !24)
    ; apply-test(!"list-fold 5", list-fold(mul-helper | 0), ![1, 2, 3, 4], !0)

    end
-----------------------------------------------------------

Unfortunately, these helper strategies cannot be defined anonymously,
as in Haskell etc.

Hope this helps. The chunking example might require even lower-level
use, perhaps you will have to  avoid making a tuple to carry the size
of the current chunk.

(Note that you can always resort to writing a bit of C code: the
native interface of Stratego is very easy to use).

Cheers,
-- 
Martin Bravenboer
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Department of Computer Science
University of Massachusetts Amherst

In fact, we tried using the term argument,

On Thu, Feb 12, 2009 at 6:06 PM, Martin Bravenboer
<martin.bravenboer at gmail.com> wrote:
> Hi Sander,
>
>> Did I miss something here? Or does anyone know a better way of dealing
>> with large lists?
>
> I'm not sure it's a wise idea to use ATerm lists for this, but
> list-fold should at least be fairly efficient in terms of memory.
> List-fold was introduced to avoid the creation of intermediate tuples,
> as the other fold strategies do. List-fold a normal fold, where the
> strategy parameter is a strategy taking a term argument. The example
> from the testsuite will probably clarify this:
>
> -----------------------------------------------------------
> ?list-fold-tests =
> ? ?let add-helper(|x) = <add> (x, <id>)
> ? ? ? ?mul-helper(|x) = <mul> (x, <id>)
> ? ? in id
>
> ? ?; apply-test(!"list-fold 1", list-fold(add-helper | 0), ![], !0)
> ? ?; apply-test(!"list-fold 2", list-fold(add-helper | 0), ![1], !1)
> ? ?; apply-test(!"list-fold 3", list-fold(add-helper | 0), ![1, 2, 3, 4], !10)
> ? ?; apply-test(!"list-fold 4", list-fold(mul-helper | 1), ![1, 2, 3, 4], !24)
> ? ?; apply-test(!"list-fold 5", list-fold(mul-helper | 0), ![1, 2, 3, 4], !0)
>
> ? ?end
> -----------------------------------------------------------
>
> Unfortunately, these helper strategies cannot be defined anonymously,
> as in Haskell etc.
>
> Hope this helps. The chunking example might require even lower-level
> use, perhaps you will have to ?avoid making a tuple to carry the size
> of the current chunk.
>
> (Note that you can always resort to writing a bit of C code: the
> native interface of Stratego is very easy to use).
>
> Cheers,
> --
> Martin Bravenboer

> Department of Computer Science

want to use that. I suspect it won't work. The error seems related to

and Nix has moved: http://nixos.org

The Stratego/XT website has links to the relevant integration builds etc :)

From karltk at strategoxt.org  Wed Feb 18 11:49:35 2009
From: karltk at strategoxt.org (Karl Trygve Kalleberg)
Date: Wed, 18 Feb 2009 11:49:35 +0100
Subject: [Stratego Users] IRC channel tips (was: Re: Help with Dryad-front)
In-Reply-To: <000601c991b2$746d82f0$7a01010a@CSE.local>
References: <ed7b6cf90902160640m3abe4e60v2c65903eb6e6603f@mail.gmail.com><001601c990ed$c15cc0a0$ad0ca8c0@CSE.local>	<ed7b6cf90902170312v3fcd0deav80396e955a465918@mail.gmail.com>
	<000601c991b2$746d82f0$7a01010a@CSE.local>
Message-ID: <499BE7BF.10406@strategoxt.org>

dflynn wrote:

> Also you may want to try the IRC channel, it is
> supposed to be a better way of receiving help on these issues, I am 
> planning to do the same.

IRC has the big advantage of being near realtime interactive. However, 
relevant expertise might not be at hand at the precise moment you show 
up. Nevertheless, please state your question (asking if you can ask is 
superfluous -- just ask). If you don't get a reply, restate it a couple 
of hours later, or if people you suspect might know anything have joined 
in the meantime.

The mailing list is an obvious fallback if IRC proves fruitless.

We try to answer as many questions as we can, both on IRC and the 
mailing list, but sometimes we're engaged with fixing bugs or doing some 
research, too;P


Cheers,

-- Karl T

From E.Visser at tudelft.nl  Wed Feb 25 16:01:52 2009
From: E.Visser at tudelft.nl (Eelco Visser)
Date: Wed, 25 Feb 2009 16:01:52 +0100
Subject: [Stratego Users] MODELS + GPCE + SLE in Denver
Message-ID: <1235574112.10975.38.camel@dutiga>


If you're doing research into domain-specific languages, model-driven
engineering, or program generation, your agenda for the coming months is
set. Early October the three main conferences on these topics are
co-located in Denver. The deadlines are somewhat spread, so you should
be able to submit a paper to each conference: 

May 10:  Model Driven Engineering Languages and Systems (MODELS'09)
         http://www.modelsconference.org/

May 18:  Generative Programming and Component Engineering (GPCE'09)
         http://www.hope.cs.rice.edu/twiki/bin/view/GPCE09

July 10: Software Language Engineering (SLE 2009)
         http://planet-sl.org/sle2009/

I'm looking forward to your submission, and to meeting you in Denver. 

cheers,

-- Eelco
http://eelcovisser.org
